  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8ff9c135-f9f2-4220-8aef-de6b4ec6e39b'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer15034880603735554045">Jack and Melissa McGuane have spent years trying to have a baby. Finally their dream has come true with the adoption of their daughter, Angelina. But nine months after bringing her home, they receive a devastating phone call…<br/><br/>Angelina's birth father, a teenager, never signed away his parental rights—and he wants her back.   <span id="freeText15034880603735554045" style="display:none">Jack and Melissa McGuane have spent years trying to have a baby. Finally their dream has come true with the adoption of their daughter, Angelina. But nine months after bringing her home, they receive a devastating phone call…<br /><br />Angelina's birth father, a teenager, never signed away his parental rights—and he wants her back. Worse, his father, a powerful Denver judge, will use every trick in the book to make sure it happens. The McGuanes attempt to meet face-to-face with the father and son…but soon it becomes clear that there's something sinister about their motivations—and that love for Angelina is not one of them.<br /><br />A horrifying game of intimidation and double crosses begins that quickly becomes a death spiral where everyone is suspect and no one is safe. Now Jack and Melissa will stop at nothing to protect their child—even though time is running out…</span>

    <a title="Melinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4870710-melinda"><img alt="Melinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523499319p2/4870710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/700953591?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda" href="/user/show/4870710-melinda">Melinda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4870710-melinda?shelf=wall-of-shame">wall-of-shame</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer700953591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13252557831877922913">Oh, lord. The plot was predictable, the whole thing was so cliche it made me want to throw it out the window. The writing was terrible. The characters nothing more than stereotypes. You have an evil super powerful judge and his sociopathic gangster son, the beloved gay best friend of the family, the loyal family dog (guess what happens there), the burned out alcoholic cop friend, the very moral but sexy beautiful wife who is a saint of a mother, Uncle Jeter the big hearted thug who will pound yo</span>
  <span id="freeText13252557831877922913" style="display:none">Oh, lord. The plot was predictable, the whole thing was so cliche it made me want to throw it out the window. The writing was terrible. The characters nothing more than stereotypes. You have an evil super powerful judge and his sociopathic gangster son, the beloved gay best friend of the family, the loyal family dog (guess what happens there), the burned out alcoholic cop friend, the very moral but sexy beautiful wife who is a saint of a mother, Uncle Jeter the big hearted thug who will pound your enemies for you, and the strong protective husband who is crazy in love with his wife. Ugh. Even baby Angelina, who spends all of her time either sleeping (so the adults can talk) or "gurgling happily", smiling and laughing, charming everyone (strangers included) and displaying delightful behavior that is not normal for a baby under a year old and waaaaay too cute. I don't even want to finish this review. I am still too annoyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13252557831877922913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45465975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45465975" />
    <a title="LJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/250195-lj"><img alt="LJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436467895p2/250195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45465975" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9569424981664338389">THREE WEEKS TO SAY GOODBYE (Thriller-Jack and Melissa McGuane-CO-Cont) - Poor<br/>Box, C.J. – Standalone<br/>St. Martin’s Minotaur, 2009, US Hardcover – ISBN: 9780312365721<br/><br/>First Sentence: It was Saturday morning, November 3, and the first thing I noticed when I entered my office was that my telephone message light was blinking.<br/><br/>Jack and Melissa McGuane finally have the child they longed for having adopted Angelina nine months ago. Their dream has become a nightmare as they are told the baby’s father never </span>
  <span id="freeText9569424981664338389" style="display:none">THREE WEEKS TO SAY GOODBYE (Thriller-Jack and Melissa McGuane-CO-Cont) - Poor<br />Box, C.J. – Standalone<br />St. Martin’s Minotaur, 2009, US Hardcover – ISBN: 9780312365721<br /><br />First Sentence: It was Saturday morning, November 3, and the first thing I noticed when I entered my office was that my telephone message light was blinking.<br /><br />Jack and Melissa McGuane finally have the child they longed for having adopted Angelina nine months ago. Their dream has become a nightmare as they are told the baby’s father never signed away his parental rights. It’s not, they find, the boy who wants the child, but his father. <br /><br />Judge John Moreland is wealthy, powerful and very connected in Denver and beyond. What he wants, he generally gets, and he has the law on his side. It is clear there is no way Jack and Melissa and fight Moreland within the system. With the help of two of his childhood friends, they find the son runs with gang members, the Judge is not as upstanding as he appears and the combination is very dangerous.<br /><br />It is so frustrating when you are a fan of an author’s writing, and then they disappoint. Box is a very good writer. His style was there; the ability to draw the reader in from the beginning, increasing the tension with every step and bringing it to a dramatic climax. The sense of place was strong and the dialogue worked. <br /><br />What let me down; was the plot and the characters. Hackneyed and ludicrous are words that come to mind for the plot. The story was so contrived and I knew where it was going every step along the way. There were no surprises. The characters were black or while; there were no shades of gray at all. <br /><br />They only thing that remotely saved it for me was the last chapter. If you are looking for an airplane book to distract you for a few hours, this will do. If you are expecting something up to Box’s usual standard, I expect you will be very disappointed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9569424981664338389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText71468747415205713" style="display:none">I read this book in one sitting, from 8pm to midnight, even though the story wasn't really good. I liked the premise, a young couple has adopted a baby, only to learn that the teenage father never signed away his parental rights. The young man's father decides his son needs to own up to his responsibility, and they want the baby. But there's something off about the man and his son, and the child might be in danger. <br /><br />As I read, the danger facing the child seemed contrived. Instead of working through the legal system, the adoptive parents try to buy off the kid, which doesn't work since his father is a wealthy federal judge. So then they hire a crazed mountain man, the uncle of one of their best friends, as a hit man. Another friend tries to dig up dirt through his network of society friends, and is later beaten to death for his involvement. As it turns out, the judge is involved in a convuluted blackmail scheme with a pedophile, and the baby is part of his payoff. The situation comes to a head during the exchange- baby for incriminating evidence, and the adoptive father is there with his cop friends to save the day. Really? </span>

<div id="review_81372839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81372839" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/133202-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294082070p2/133202.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81372839?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/133202-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312365738" href="/book/show/6370557-three-weeks-to-say-goodbye">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/133202-erin?shelf=crime-suspense">crime-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81372839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3441893481583976983">I'd probably bump this up to 2.5 stars, but this book just didn't work for me. I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1395807.Blue_Heaven' title='Blue Heaven by C.J. Box' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blue Heaven</a>, and i think I was expecting something similar. I think authors make their antagonists more interesting when they have realistic (but flawed or bad) motives. The cops in Blue Heaven were bad guys, but bad guys that grew cold and cynical and ugly over the years. The bad guys in Three Weeks were just...evil. Evil for no particular reason except that they were, I don't know, born that way? And that ma</span>
  <span id="freeText3441893481583976983" style="display:none">I'd probably bump this up to 2.5 stars, but this book just didn't work for me. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1395807.Blue_Heaven" title="Blue Heaven by C.J. Box" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Heaven</a>, and i think I was expecting something similar. I think authors make their antagonists more interesting when they have realistic (but flawed or bad) motives. The cops in Blue Heaven were bad guys, but bad guys that grew cold and cynical and ugly over the years. The bad guys in Three Weeks were just...evil. Evil for no particular reason except that they were, I don't know, born that way? And that made the story infinitely more tedious to me. The writing didn't flow as easily either--it just felt choppy and ungainly. <br /><br />Jack and Melissa McGuane have adopted a baby. At 9 months old, she's the love of their life, until the agency says Whoops! Sorry for the screw up! The teenage father didn't sign the adoption papers! 18-year old Garrett, who I think is your standard teen sociopath, gets his father, a Federal Court judge, involved in this mess and he tells the McGuanes they have, you guessed it, Three Weeks To Say Goodbye to baby Angelina. But of course, both the baby daddy AND his father are not what they seem (cue mustache-twirling evil), and Jack needs to take them down before they take away his baby. In 3 weeks. Hopefully without killings someone in a fit of rage and going to jail. And then there's a subplot regarding Jack's job that is somewhat related, but mostly uninteresting, and I just couldn't get too attached to anyone in particular. Which was too bad, because I totally wanted to! But I couldn't! So, blah. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3441893481583976983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_56696828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56696828" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1383959-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297176343p2/1383959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56696828?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/1383959-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves a good thriller.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dawn by: </span>
      I loved C. J. Box's other book "Blue Heaven".
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56696828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer149797301194864789">Another fast paced, edge of your seat thriller by C. J. Box. I absolutely loved his book "Blue Heaven" and was anxious to read this one. "Three Weeks To Say Goodbye" did not disappoint. The story keeps moving along and you never know what is going to happen next. This story would make a great movie too. I've enjoyed both of his "stand alone" books so much, I may have to read his others that are part of a series. I highly recommend this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14162757994680837361" style="display:none">It’s all too much.<br /><br />A couple discovers they have to give up their adopted baby because the birth father did not sign away his parental rights. Interesting premise. Then it all falls apart.<br /><br />Don’t worry, no spoilers here: The birth father turns out to be a teenager – but not any kind of teenager; a dark brooding teenager. But not any kind of dark brooding teenager; a dark brooding teenager who doesn’t “get along with dogs”, has a suspicious past, has gang ties and is the son of a judge. But not any kind of judge; a super powerful Federal judge. But not any kind of super powerful Federal judge; a sinister super powerful Federal judge with secrets to hide… <br /><br />The psycho-teen taunts and spooks the family with his strange behaviours, warning them that they had to “keep him happy” or he won’t sign the papers saying things like “I own you now”… <br /><br />So, the parents decide to “do everything they can to save their child”, start their own investigation and high octane action ensues, twists and turns and murders and intrigue and double crosses…ARGH! ENOUGH! it was just too over-the-top for me.</span>

  <span id="freeText6109541045615033988" style="display:none">Jack and Melissa McGuane try having a baby. They can't. They adopt Angelina. Nine months after bringing her home, they receive news that the biological father wants his daughter back. The McGuane's find out the last thing Angelina's birth father has for his daughter is love. Jack and Melissa will stop at nothing to protect their child.<br /><br />As an adoptive father myself, this story takes on a personal tone. I can't imagine anyone of my nine adopted children would be taken away from us. The closest we came to an understanding that was during an adoption process. The two kids we were adopting had been with us for over a year. We almost weren't able to adopt.<br /><br />Very good story. I felt the tension. Sensed the pain. Experienced the pain. The ripping of the heart was in every scene. Gripping all the way until the end. </span>

<div id="review_2516627546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2516627546" />
    <a title="Dick Reynolds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10283403-dick-reynolds"><img alt="Dick Reynolds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339956123p2/10283403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2516627546?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dick Reynolds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dick Reynolds" href="/user/show/10283403-dick-reynolds">Dick Reynolds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2516627546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1784166237497647492">	Jack and Melissa McGuane are parents of a nine month old girl named Angelina whom they adopted. Angelina’s birth mother signed the release papers but the birth father didn’t because he couldn’t be found.<br/>	The McGuane family are suddenly thrust into the center of an emotional hurricane when a young Garrett Morland appears. He’s Angelina’s birth father and wants custody of his daughter even though he doesn’t have a job and is really not interested in being a caring father. To complicate matters fu</span>
  <span id="freeText1784166237497647492" style="display:none">	Jack and Melissa McGuane are parents of a nine month old girl named Angelina whom they adopted. Angelina’s birth mother signed the release papers but the birth father didn’t because he couldn’t be found.<br />	The McGuane family are suddenly thrust into the center of an emotional hurricane when a young Garrett Morland appears. He’s Angelina’s birth father and wants custody of his daughter even though he doesn’t have a job and is really not interested in being a caring father. To complicate matters further, Garrett’s dad is John Morland, a well known and respected judge who is helping Garrett with all the relevant legal matters because he has his own agenda which involves making Angelina part of the larger Morland family.<br />	Needless to say, Jack and Melissa decide to fight the Morlands so that their beloved Angelina is not given up to a low-life like Garrett. They make a plan and one of their first steps is to learn more about Judge Morland. Jack gets a seat during a criminal trial against a man named Aubrey Coates who is accused of kidnapping and murder of a five year old girl named Courtney Wingate. The police detective who is testifying for the prosecution is one of author C. J. Box’s regular characters, Cody Hoyt. We’ve seen Cody in other novels, notably The Highway and Back of Beyond. Cody has a rough time on the witness stand, thanks to rulings by Judge Morland about his mishandling of evidence.<br />	Jack must make a business trip to Berlin and, while he’s there, the McGaune’s dog Harry is viciously poisoned. Garrett Morland is the likely suspect. When Jack returns, the family joins forces with Cody and they make a trip to Montana to meet with Cody’s uncle Jeter Hoyt. Jeter packs a lot of hardware when he comes to Denver. He shoots up the Zuni saloon and manages to kill several gang members but the intended target, Garrett Morland escapes.<br />	The forces of law close in on the McGuane family in a tension filled ending to this family drama.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1784166237497647492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143582873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143582873" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1177534-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593697601p2/1177534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143582873?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1177534-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312365738" href="/book/show/6370557-three-weeks-to-say-goodbye">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143582873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4223253544326211691">Jack and Melissa McGuane experience every adoption family's worst nightmare when just their nearly nine-month-old daughter is about to be declared legally their child, the birth father shows up and demands her back. Seems that his father, a powerful federal circuit court judge wants to teach the young man a lesson about responsibility. Or so he says upon first meeting the McGuanes and giving them a three week deadline to turn over Angelina to them. (He will, of course, compensate them for the co</span>
  <span id="freeText4223253544326211691" style="display:none">Jack and Melissa McGuane experience every adoption family's worst nightmare when just their nearly nine-month-old daughter is about to be declared legally their child, the birth father shows up and demands her back. Seems that his father, a powerful federal circuit court judge wants to teach the young man a lesson about responsibility. Or so he says upon first meeting the McGuanes and giving them a three week deadline to turn over Angelina to them. (He will, of course, compensate them for the costs of adopting the child and offers to help them find another baby to adopt).<br /><br />The father is a well connected political figure in the Denver community, leaving the couple on their own quickly. Their lawyer dumps them (he doesn't want to cross the powerful, rising star judge) and every avenue they pursue comes up empty. <br /><br />But something sinister is going on. The son shows up with his gang-banger friends to watch the Broncos/Raiders game and is taking an unusual interest in Melissa. The McGuanes, with the help of Jack's two best friends, slowly begin to delve into what the real motive for the Judge's sudden interest in their daughter is and why he's willing to use all his influence to make sure he gets the baby back.<br /><br />The first half of C.J. Box's "Three Weeks to Say Goodbye" reads like every adopted parent or family member's worst nightmare. Box paints a picture of a couple desperate to be parents and who have mortgaged their present and future to adopt Angelina. Add to it the bonds created in the eight plus months they've been parents to Angelina and you've got a truly nightmarish scenario unfolding. And that's before the couple begins to get the vibe that something else is unfolding here--something far more sinister and connected to several of the other subplots of the book.<br /><br />In fact, there's no such thing as a subplot in this book. All of the threads running through the first 50 pages all come home to roost in the final pages of the story, each with a varying degree of believability. Described by one reviewer as an elaborate "revenge story," "Three Weeks," is sort of that and sort of a suspense thriller. It's got a lot of promise and an intriguing hook. I'm just not sure it necessarily earned its ending after the final page was turned. <br /><br />As I said before, there are no loose threads here. And while some things unfolded in a different manor that I originally guessed, a lot of the revelations in the final pages didn't necessarily come as a huge surprise.<br /><br />What I was left with is mixed feelings. The first half is a fun, engaging pop-corn novel. But like many big budget Hollywood thrillers, the story tries too hard to keep piling on twist after twist, moment after moment in the second half and ends up losing a lot of the early momentum from the novel's first half. Overall, not a terrible book but not a great one either. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4223253544326211691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2447107235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447107235" />
    <a title="Brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72028192-brooke"><img alt="Brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511629558p2/72028192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447107235?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/72028192-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72028192-brooke?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447107235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12473345751918895785">I'm gonna be honest- I made it to page seventeen. It's one of my personal pet peeves when I recommend a book to someone and they give it up immediately, but this was physically painful. The tone was identical to that of textbook- there were no metaphors, no word play, no poeticism what so ever (and believe me when I say that my teenage angsty ass is crazed for poeticism). There was essentially no introduction. We just went straight into the main plot, which some may like, but I want some actual </span>
  <span id="freeText12473345751918895785" style="display:none">I'm gonna be honest- I made it to page seventeen. It's one of my personal pet peeves when I recommend a book to someone and they give it up immediately, but this was physically painful. The tone was identical to that of textbook- there were no metaphors, no word play, no poeticism what so ever (and believe me when I say that my teenage angsty ass is crazed for poeticism). There was essentially no introduction. We just went straight into the main plot, which some may like, but I want some actual context and character development before any major events. I would have also like to see some insight on how much Jack and Melissa loved their daughter and how hard they worked to get her BEFORE the news of a custody issue so I could experience more of an emotional impact from the thought of them losing their baby. I wish I could give the pace a speeding ticket. Not only did it go right into it, but it was just major event, after major event, after major event (in the FIRST SEVENTEEN PAGES). The only instance between major events was awkward, yet unrealistically saccharine dialogue. Everything said feels like these characters know EXACTLY what to say to accommodate some plot. Not to mention, with the character Garrett, I think C.J. Box has a lot of problems with teenagers walking across his lawn. I know, teenagers can be assholes (written by a girl who just graduated middle school), but he made it out like because of his age, Garrett had no soul or conscience at all. My immediate mental picture of him was literally a classic black-wearing, apathetic, shaggy-haired, drug-addicted, secretly violent teen from the works of a Disney Channel movie about bullying or a horribly misleading school shooting PSA. And of course my guy, C.J. has to look like the sex offender Louis C.K.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12473345751918895785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_61636357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Liberty Abbott-Sylvester" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457001-liberty-abbott-sylvester"><img alt="Liberty Abbott-Sylvester" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572978993p2/2457001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61636357?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liberty Abbott-Sylvester" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liberty Abbott-Sylvester" href="/user/show/2457001-liberty-abbott-sylvester">Liberty Abbott-Sylvester</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61636357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2735340800890245413">This book was fantastic. It had my attention from page one. The characters are lovable and you are easily drawn into their dilemma. Imagine someone coming to take your child away in three weeks! Wow!<br/>There were parts where I wanted to cry and parts I just got mad about.This is a very quick read and I'm glad I found it. I'll be reading more by CJ Box!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10772876061061729559">A very different C J Box book. This is a compelling story of young parents in an impossible situation. <br/><br/>Having adopted a son, I know what this couple was facing. Having a foster son for a year, I remember what it felt like when we were told our time was up. <br/><br/>Mr. Box has it exactly right. <br/><br/>This is a tough story with an incredible end. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >

Now picture receiving a phone call from the adoption agency informing you that the "birth father" want his child. This is where the story begins. There are many twists and turns in this story. Intrigue, murder, you name the crimes and it's in this book. Read it!</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8003791557646471221">Older standalone novel by author Box<br/><br/>I bought this book recently because I thought it was one of Box's books I hadn't read - and I've read all of his other books. Once I got started on this one, it kept getting more familiar and I realized I'd read it when it first came out in 2009. It was no hardship though because I enjoyed it again.<br/><br/>I do have to write that it's a different writing style than the author's other books. This is more of a mainstream thriller.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the characters and the story w</span>
  <span id="freeText8003791557646471221" style="display:none">Older standalone novel by author Box<br /><br />I bought this book recently because I thought it was one of Box's books I hadn't read - and I've read all of his other books. Once I got started on this one, it kept getting more familiar and I realized I'd read it when it first came out in 2009. It was no hardship though because I enjoyed it again.<br /><br />I do have to write that it's a different writing style than the author's other books. This is more of a mainstream thriller.<br /><br />I enjoyed the characters and the story was heartbreaking. I tried to imagine if something like this happened to me. What would I do? How far would I go to protect a child of mine?<br /><br />It is action packed and was hard to put down. As his other books, I heartily recommend this tale from Box.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6018062070364436383">it could happen - if the adoptee's don't both sign the papers no matter how long the adopters have the child, she or he can be returned. Sinister judge and sociopathic son decide after 14 months the baby is to be returned to them. The adopters, a young, happy couple who dote on the baby are crushed and as time goes on learn horrible things about ugly facts concerning the welfare of their child if turned over to biological father. Scary...the countdown...</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RVAsyVXcA6bqLQqi7kLDsuknIxUG1QckVu60RpOkY+36V0Y4eDg/KXglnaz1Lf9RQguvcfUDP9KPKqafzV1UPA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TSsfs96bJAZKLZ4qixPsKo/q3H6aBfhyA6azRoG0W2PyLHVC838YidglCSSQfNDJJMZQGmnTwITaYqGf301ssg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18289448590468488987">C. J. Box is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of 24 novels including the Joe Pickett series. He won the Edgar Alan Poe Award for Best Novel (Blue Heaven, 2009) as well as the Anthony Award, Prix Calibre 38 (France), the Macavity Award, the Gumshoe Award, two Barry Awards, and the 2010 Mountains & Plains Independent Booksellers Association Award for fiction. He was recently awarded the 2016</span>
  <span id="freeText18289448590468488987" style="display:none">C. J. Box is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of 24 novels including the Joe Pickett series. He won the Edgar Alan Poe Award for Best Novel (Blue Heaven, 2009) as well as the Anthony Award, Prix Calibre 38 (France), the Macavity Award, the Gumshoe Award, two Barry Awards, and the 2010 Mountains &amp; Plains Independent Booksellers Association Award for fiction. He was recently awarded the 2016 Western Heritage Award for Literature by the National Cowboy Museum as well as the Spur Award for Best Contemporary Novel by the Western Writers of America in 2017. The novels have been translated into 27 languages. <br /><br />Box is a Wyoming native and has worked as a ranch hand, surveyor, fishing guide, a small town newspaper reporter and editor, and he co-owns an international tourism marketing firm with his wife Laurie. They have three daughters. An avid outdoorsman, Box has hunted, fished, hiked, ridden, and skied throughout Wyoming and the Mountain West. He served on the Board of Directors for the Cheyenne Frontier Days Rodeo. Box lives in Wyoming.<br /><br /><i>--from the author's website</i><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41706-joe-pickett" rel="nofollow noopener">Joe Pickett</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/cjbox">http://us.macmillan.com/author/cjbox</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18289448590468488987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

But they chose to be good, even if what they did could be questioned within the strict confines of the law.&rdquo;</span>
